<div id="review_2852182992" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2852182992" />
    <a title="erica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2796628-erica"><img alt="erica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571003113p2/2796628.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2852182992?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="erica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="erica" href="/user/show/2796628-erica">erica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2796628-erica?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2796628-erica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2852182992" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2037362886958524582">This was unfortunate. <br/><br/>I read the first book in this series, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7896345.The_Gathering__Darkness_Rising___1_' title='The Gathering (Darkness Rising, #1) by Kelley Armstrong' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Gathering</a>, last week and I really enjoyed it - the setting, the magic/science, the First Nations rep, the shapeshifting. <i>The Calling</i> picks up exactly where <i>The Gathering</i> left off but you don't need to read it <i>immediately</i> after the first book because Armstrong gives us a solid two-page summary (which is mildly annoying, but whatever). <br/><br/><i>The Calling</i> showcases Armstrong's poor writing skills. This book has zero plot - it's completely dri</span>
  <span id="freeText2037362886958524582" style="display:none">This was unfortunate. <br /><br />I read the first book in this series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7896345.The_Gathering__Darkness_Rising___1_" title="The Gathering (Darkness Rising, #1) by Kelley Armstrong" rel="nofollow noopener">The Gathering</a>, last week and I really enjoyed it - the setting, the magic/science, the First Nations rep, the shapeshifting. <i>The Calling</i> picks up exactly where <i>The Gathering</i> left off but you don't need to read it <i>immediately</i> after the first book because Armstrong gives us a solid two-page summary (which is mildly annoying, but whatever). <br /><br /><i>The Calling</i> showcases Armstrong's poor writing skills. This book has zero plot - it's completely driven by action (which is terribly written itself). This series is a trilogy, but this book should have been dropped entirely, leaving us with a duology. Nothing new happens here - it's all about running around in the woods and hiding from the bad guys. We learn absolutely nothing new - not about the world, the magic/mystery, or the characters. <i>Nothing</i>. And the plot is so basic and uninteresting that we know <i>exactly</i> what will happen in the third book. Instead of writing according to the basic YA trilogy format I wish Armstrong had edited this book down to a few chapters and stuck them in the other two books. <br /><br />Will I read the next book in the series? Part of me thinks I might as well - it's sure to be a quick read, and I hate leaving series unfinished (especially when there's only one book left!). But <i>The Calling</i> is shockingly bad - Armstrong shows just how unimaginative and uninspired she is, and I am confident I know exactly how the series will end. Life is short and we should spend our time reading books we enjoy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2037362886958524582" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3037920935142251313">I have a 73 page rule where if I can't get into the book after about 73 pages I stop reading it. While I hate the idea that I spent money on a book I'm not going to finish, there are too many good books out there to waste time reading ones that I don't really like or can't get into. That happened with this book. I got about 100 pages in and became bored. I put it down a few weeks ago and am not sure if I'm going to go back to it. It's disappointing because I really like Kelley Armstrong - she's </span>
  <span id="freeText3037920935142251313" style="display:none">I have a 73 page rule where if I can't get into the book after about 73 pages I stop reading it. While I hate the idea that I spent money on a book I'm not going to finish, there are too many good books out there to waste time reading ones that I don't really like or can't get into. That happened with this book. I got about 100 pages in and became bored. I put it down a few weeks ago and am not sure if I'm going to go back to it. It's disappointing because I really like Kelley Armstrong - she's one of my favorite authors. But I just can't get into the Darkness Rising series. I had some hesitance in buying this book because I wasn't sure how I felt about the first book in the series. Now that I'm feeling the same way about the second book, I think this is a series that I won't be finishing. I'm sure a lot of people loved it since Kelley is such a great writer but I just wasn't feeling this one.</span>

<div id="review_917354235" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/917354235" />
    <a title="Nathalie*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15545359-nathalie"><img alt="Nathalie*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486475801p2/15545359.jpg" /></a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2174948524?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Plot Monster" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Plot Monster" href="/user/show/61724382-plot-monster">Plot Monster</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2174948524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13833999992450604792">The Calling by Kelley Armstrong has 326 pages and was published in 2012 by Harper.<br/><br/>In the Calling, Maya and co are kidnapped in a helicopter that ultimately crashes.  After, surviving the crash, they spend the majority of the book running from the bad guys.  <br/><br/>While I enjoyed the first book in this series, this one was a little bit of a let down.  It started out good.  It held promise.  Unfortunately, this book simply did not live up to the hype.  The story of the stranded kids in the wilderness ju</span>
  <span id="freeText13833999992450604792" style="display:none">The Calling by Kelley Armstrong has 326 pages and was published in 2012 by Harper.<br /><br />In the Calling, Maya and co are kidnapped in a helicopter that ultimately crashes.  After, surviving the crash, they spend the majority of the book running from the bad guys.  <br /><br />While I enjoyed the first book in this series, this one was a little bit of a let down.  It started out good.  It held promise.  Unfortunately, this book simply did not live up to the hype.  The story of the stranded kids in the wilderness just seemed to drag on and on and on and on...  You get the idea.While there was a lot of action in this book, the story itself (and the characters) needed to be fleshed out a bit more, in my humble opinion.  <br /><br />Kelley Armstrong is an incredibly gifted author and I have enjoyed every book I have read that she authored - including this one.  I just think perhaps this was not her best work.<br /><br />Recommended for fans of the Darkest Powers trilogy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13833999992450604792" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3762766481715138068">I really love the characters, and how they're all tight knit. But Maya's constant revelations about how she had maybe been wrong about the people she had grew up with, and maybe she wasn't such a good judge of character were annoying. Some parts were way too predictable and convenient. I also hated how it seemed the characters were intentionally acting stupid just to have some sort of conflict.<br/> <br/>I love that the story is a little bit different from other books that I've read about shifters. It see</span>
  <span id="freeText3762766481715138068" style="display:none">I really love the characters, and how they're all tight knit. But Maya's constant revelations about how she had maybe been wrong about the people she had grew up with, and maybe she wasn't such a good judge of character were annoying. Some parts were way too predictable and convenient. I also hated how it seemed the characters were intentionally acting stupid just to have some sort of conflict.<br /> <br />I love that the story is a little bit different from other books that I've read about shifters. It seems original, and I love the characters.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('43L7lmuDG+ldHO/3QXmfGXpvIU9KeDeiEycMFUXBRHwTy0X+9Lt5x2Dp2+1Ep4meHifugJuGqmLRKlU7MJgkWw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Q9MnZJzxHkqqbXyixsHVMj+obJvmC5QCFv8Y02/EFBGzapkMA8l8ZJeYSLjDH8O1W+CjVDf1CcLU8kH9Gp10Ng==')})
  }
//]]>

<span id="freeTextContainer17124839757436303481">Kelley Armstrong has been telling stories since before she could write. Her earliest written efforts were disastrous. If asked for a story about girls and dolls, hers would invariably feature undead girls and evil dolls, much to her teachers' dismay. All efforts to make her produce "normal" stories failed.<br/><br/>Today, she continues to spin tales of ghosts and demons and werewolves, while safely locked a</span>
  <span id="freeText17124839757436303481" style="display:none">Kelley Armstrong has been telling stories since before she could write. Her earliest written efforts were disastrous. If asked for a story about girls and dolls, hers would invariably feature undead girls and evil dolls, much to her teachers' dismay. All efforts to make her produce "normal" stories failed.<br /><br />Today, she continues to spin tales of ghosts and demons and werewolves, while safely locked away in her basement writing dungeon. She's the author of the NYT-bestselling "Women of the Otherworld" paranormal suspense series and "Darkest Powers" young adult urban fantasy trilogy, as well as the Nadia Stafford crime series. Armstrong lives in southwestern Ontario with her husband, kids and far too many pets. <br /><br /></span>
